(1861-2387 mMD)\n\nThe lower interval (1955-2387m) of the unit is composed of brown slightly calcareous moderate brown claystone, subplaty to sublaminar, irregular fracture. In part intercalated with massive, slightly calcareous, with micropryite fossils, scarce glauconitic, siltstone.Flutolfaction of siltstone (same as described in the shalves analysis) and grey mica (locally common in siltstone). From 22251m- thin (few inches up to few dm) thick very fine light grey sandstone. Few dm interbeds of fine to medium (angular and spherical with prevailing quartz). Locally, fine gray conglomerate with clay stone matrix occurs, shale sequence is interrupted by fine to very fine grained, very well sorted intervals. Thin levels of white to medium grey, buff-blocky, platte sandstone, and siltstone, with quartz inclusions. Thin levels of light brown (limonitic) at 2127m-2134m. With calcite veining, minor iron impregnation and gray glauconite limestone, sublaminar, massive, micrite, without micro pyrite moderate hard, hard, dark gray argillaceous limestone. \n\nThe upper interval (1861-1955m) is composed of grayish-brown moderate brown partially silicifed siltstone, blocky to sublaminar, irregular fracture, fossil with pyrite, with glauconite, abundant micropyrtype, scarce coal, very slight calcareous reaction, firm. Light gray argillaceous siltstone beds to subblocky, massive, irregular fracture, firm to massive, sand stained and interbedded with thin la,yer laminated limestones.\n\nR\xc3\xado Mayer Inf. (1837-2482 mMD)\n\nThis Formation is represented by medium dark gray in far brown (1955-2387m) hard siltstone, blocky, irregular fracture, occasional pyrite inclusions, some scattered fine intercalations of calcic, locally fine to medium quartizitic sand grains, firm to blocky with some stone intervals. In minor part intercalation of buff brown siltstone, non-calcareous, massive to soft, blocky. Subtotally gray massive intercalations of fine greyish siltstone, firm to blocky. From 2465 to 2482m, brown flat dark brown micaceous limestone. The base of the section is characterized by fine, hard, abundant glauconite, with traces of white and little brown fine sand, with white fine calcite vein. At 2470- 2482m- buff brown claystone, partially limestone. The deepest meters are represented by very light gray siltstone and silty claystone, with sides, being blocky, conglomeratic, subangular, flat ironed, quartzitic, very gray brown siltstone, gray to brown slightly argillaceous matrix, hard, totally fine, fair porosity. \n\nAGUA SQUENCE (2471-2482mMD)\n\nThe sequence begins at the base with brown black claystone with darker brown siltstone beds of the base of the conglomerate and brownish blocky ironed grey micrinite.SHIDRI (2488-2485m MD)\n\nGeographical sequence can be identified: the basal OSS.\n\nThe basal OSS (2488-2485m) is composed of basal to very coarse sand and gravel which grades from medium to coarse, with alternation of brown blocky siltstone, both with gradual contacts (three intervals of core inclusions).\n\nThe middle interval (2519,40m) is composed of coarse to very coarse gravelly sand. The gravel is contained by a fine grained conglomerate which has abundant greenish silty clay matrix. Small portion of fine to very fine grained black siltstone can be identified.\n\nThe top interval (2502ft/9ft), again in part a conglomerate (basal sequence, with the major portions transitioning of brown to pale green to medium grained banded siltstone, with the same matrix as the lower intervals.\n\nTowards the top, thin beds of coarse gravel sand grade upwards into fine quartz and sand at the top.\n\nXRD analysis indicate a higher percentage of clay minerals > 20% clays sandwiched between two dark green clay bands, including illite, smectite, and kaolinite.\n\nOverall, mineral composition analysis of the whole interval reveals very high contents of smectite with variable percentage of other clays. High clay content is usually an indicator of high swelling potential and permeabilities are very low: 0.2 in, exceptionally 10 mD.\n\nHIGHRIL SEQUENCE (26805-2550)\n\nThree base sequence are identified: the basal one.\n\nThe basal has one (26805-2535m) is composed of coarse to very coarse sand and gravel which grades from medium to coarse, with alternation of brown blocky siltstone, both with gradual contacts (three intervals of core inclusions).\n\nThe middle interval (2519,40m) is composed of coarse to very coarse gravelly sand. The gravel is contained by a fine grained conglomerate which has abundant greenish silty clay matrix (clay includes Red cans). Mainly quartzitic, minor lithics glauconite and smectite. Clay analysis: Red dominant portion of fine to very fine grained, pale green to medium grained banded siltstone.\n\nThe top interval (2502ft/9ft), again in part a conglomerate (basal sequence, with the major portions transitioning of brown to pale green to medium grained banded siltstone, with the same matrix as lower intervals.\n\nTowards the top, thin beds of coarse gravel sand grade upwards into fine quartz and sand at the top.\n\nXRD analysis indicate a higher percentage of clay minerals > 20% clays sandwiched between two dark green clay bands.\n\nGeneral analysis indicate that the major components are chloride of illite and smectite and mainly illite and kaolinite with other minor components like trioctahedrite.\n\nOverall, mineral composition analysis of the whole interval reveals very high contents of smectite with variable percentage of other clays. Clay matrix is generally of light greenish yellow tone with minor amounts of grey brown siltstone. Permeabilities are generally 10-50md up to 200md with significant quantities of the other clays. Core porosity is usually high >10%.D120-tobifera 2550/2565\n\nUpper sandy foreset: Medium to very coarse, partly conglomeradic, very light grey, subangular, poorly sorted, quartz hyaline, minor lithics, locally argillaceous matrix, fair porosity. Remaining section has small sharp light gray sandstone, medium grained, brown grey, with coal inclusions. White altered tuff at the base. (Large proportion of coaly inclusions in recovered cuttings).\n\nTobifera (2605-2650 mMD)\n\nThis Formation is composed of intercalations of white tuff, subblocky to subplaty, with lithics, firm in parts and sandy tuff. Very light gray tuffaceous silty sandstone, medium to coarse, subrounded, poor sorted, quartz hyaline, minor lithics, micropyrite, locally argillaceous matrix, friable, fair porosity and very light gray sandstone, medium to coarse, in parts conglomerate, subangular, poor sorted, quartz hyaline, minor lithics, micropyrite, locally argillaceous matrix, friable, fair porosity.\n\nIn minor part, irregular fracture with brown tuffaceous silty-claystone, blocky to subblocky, massive, hyaline altered tuff, with coal inclusions, firm.INFORMACION FALTANTE11. Thin beds of greenish/gray sandstone arenite intercalated towards the top and base of formation. The beds are very fine to medium grained, subangular-subrounded, with poor to good roundness. The beds of arenites contain glauconite, magnetite, quartz, tuff, and rare lithic fragments. Poorly cemented and with poor visual porosity, in part grading to siltstone. Also thin interbeds of tuffaceous sandstone, dolomite can be identified, specially towards the base. They are partly laterilized in the basal chalky, locally biotitic, poorly to moderately hard. Fossils traces.\n\n- Rio Leona Formation (450-541 m)\n\nThis Formation is formed mainly by light brownish gray siltstones. The siltstones are in part pyritic micaceous, friacceus, tuffaceous with pyrite, locally glauconite, quartz, dark lithics, in part sandy, firm to soft. Grading to claystone. Abundant dark gyey to black licoreal veins are identified at 470/80 m as biotitic, sub clay to plannar, soft to firm. Biote green turf belts, frequent and rare, biotite woodifyed, fossified, Pyrite in form of balls 8 to 10 inches form. Inferred and interbedded in this section.\n\n- Man Aike Formation (541-74 m)\n\nIt has two informal levels. The Basal unit (720-754m) is brownish to greenish siltstone to medium, subrounded-subangular, well to fairly sorted, and with poor to good roundness, in part with interbeds of dark gray/black, firm to soft, dolomites. The unit is very thin with rare arenite and sandstone, coarse to very coarse predominance.\n\nThe Lower Middle unit (688-721m) is formed at the top, mainly by glauconites of angular glauconite, well to fairly sorted, firm to soft, sandy, with quartz silicacrous, and dark lithic fragments added. In minor proportion, dark greenish to greenish black sandy glauconite arenaceous and glauconitewell, well sorted, quartz, firm in part, with glauconite, abundant dark lithics and lithic silica, fine to loose, fair porosity, with pyrite and few lithic fragments of black sands. Rare thick and thin to very fine grain glauconite balls.In the Middle part 625-685m, the unit is dark greenish gray to green fractured sandstone with thick intercalations of abundant glauconitic matrix, friable to well sorted, very fine grained, moderate porosity, good visible pores; local variations include the omission of lower glauconitic lithics, abundant argillaceous matrix, subrounded to subdued grains. The presence of glauconitic in the sandstone moderates the green unit, blocky to subblocky, friable to subloose, interbedded with abundant matrix, locally finr sands, silt, upper part (735-785m) dark greenish to green sandstone, containing glauconitic, well visible porosity: intercalations of brownish gray claystone levels, subsidiary to abundant, plastic, soft, calcite matrix, high porosity, local calcite spars and partially calcareous oversandstone.\n\nTowards the base, greenish gray sandstone, subangular, friable, with revising inclusions as glauconitic matrix, friable, to blocky, interbedded with very soft to softened thick unit, blackish gray sandstone, containing glauconitic, well evolved porosity, local calcite matrix, subsidiary to abundant, soft, blocky to subloose, interbedded with calcareous oversandstone.\n\nThe upper unit (887-890m) gray sandstone is formed by very tight, blocky, to very soft, soft thin own sandstone beds.This section is mainly composed of dark gray to medium to dark gray siliciclastics, with irregular fracture, microcalcareous, with micropiryte, locally with glauconite, occasional milky-coal. Grading to claystones, silstones (soft, 5-10% tuffaceous grains) grading locally to tuffaceous (soft, grading to tuffaceous claystone can be identified. Also medium light gray to medium stuffclastics can be observed in sandy-silty sorted, quartz-rich, micro- calcareous, soft to loose or poor porosity, grading to sandy tuff.\n\nMata Amarilla (936-1224 m)\n\nThis formation can be divided in four intervals. The lower section from 1110-1224 m displays dark gray, sorted and yellowish gray dark tuff gray silty claystone (described in the field as firm to medium soft and very light gray and greenish gray tuff), firm to medium soft content of 10 to 30%, microcalcareous coal, sandy and yellowish gray tuffaceous silty sandstone (medium to fine soft) with pyrite are recorded at the base of the unit. Also, locally in this section may loose, fair porosity contains glauconite at the base of the unit. Also, locally in this section may loose, fair porosity and very fine loosely compacted basal part of the unit. Also, locally in the section 1235-1234, are medium chunky gray to brownish clay claystone, blocky to sublaminar, with pyrite, microcalcareous, with faint to moderate bedding, mostly loose, soft, disaggregated.\n\nLevels of light gray sandstone can be identified at 1110-1040 m. medium to dark gray, subrounded, poorly sorted, with quartz-volcanic lithics, in part with moderate carbonate, mostly loose, and good porosity.\n\nIn the middle to top of Mata Amarilla, this gray clayey sandstone is overlain by clay silty claystone, blocky to subplaty, compact, massive, irregular fracture, with pyrite, microcalcareous with good porosity light gray tuffaceous sandstone with fine to medium tuffaceous, finely coaly content, quartz-lithic, tuffaceous matrix, intervals for 1001040 to 936-1033m.\n\nAt the top the 936-1033m, can be observed thick gray poor microcalcareous claystone and thin interbedded gray light gray turffcaous sandstone with dark brown lenses containing calcareous cement, friable, loose tuff grains, with fair porosity. Also, occasional moderately coal blocky, irregular fracture. Microcalcareous. The lower section from 1225: 1224-. can be divided in two intervals for the claystones grading to medium clayey clayoftuffaceous clayey sand.\n\nPiedra Clavada (1225-1640 m)\n\nThis section can be separated into three intervals. The lower section from 1640-1496 m displays a claystone formation, in part foliated grading to gray, silty fine-medium to dark brown, occasionally friable, firm to soft, in parts fossiliferous, with occasional microcalcareous cement.sandy turf, subblocky, quartz, micaceous, green lithics sots. Greenish-gray claystone and white to light brownish gray turf, very lightly laminated, soft, part finely fossiliferous, rarely sandy, fine to medium, subangular, poorly sorted. Rainwash on the northern side to light gray fluvial. Lower light gray to light brownish gray. Lower light gray clay turf, subblocky. gray, subblocky. Green lithics and sandstone compose the lower sandy, micaceous, irregular fractures of micaceous and the lower light gray sandstones, medium to coarse, in part fin to medium grains, with grades to flatz. Piralosi to very light sandy, white to light brownish gray meters in length.\n\nThe Middle section 1295-1500m, is composed of green silty clay turf, part calcareous, very fine to subblocky claystone, blocky to subblocky, irregular fractures, soft and sandstone layers. In part soft in places and tough in parts, part greenish black soft, subblocky clay turf, microplastic and micaceous. Grade. Very light gray. Claystone layers, in parts in places can be observed individual microlayers of black clayey clays and tufaceous sots; Very massive, firm to hard, in part carbonaceous and bituminous with the black clay streaks present throughout, with traces of coal.\n\nHave been identified from the top to two divisions turf and subblocky, developed this as part light gray tufaceous sandstone. \n\nThe upper section 1242-1295m is represented by light gray deflocculated sandstone, blocky in the lower section. Intercalations of very light gray unusual soft tites, white or light gray, with traces of coal film from poorly graded deposits. Eventually, grades of Humphrasia, deflocculated in the upper sandstone. Locally with part grades of brownish gray  up to light gray clay turf to subblocky and medium dark gray siltstone, blocky to subblocky, massive, irregular fractures, in general. Intercalations of firm gray claystone, blocky to subblocky, microplastic, irregular fractures of firm sandy, with microplastic, grades which bear moderate or lower grades otherwise with the firm gray to very tough graded small scale sots, and a sandy muddite layer fin to medium.\n\nKachia (1611-1811mMD)\n\nThis Formation is mainly composed of light gray silty shale, some beds of fine to coarse-grained, quartzose sandstone and conglomerate. The shale is mostly non-calcareous to slightly calcareous, slight calcareous content, microfossil inclusion, with glauconitic beds in the upper part; the sandstones are mostly friable, averagely sub-rounded to sub-angular, in minor part wells graded toward calcareous sandstone and conglomeratic facies frim inclusions of soft. \n\nAt the bottom from 1780m downwards increases the greenish silty to sandy content upward to mainly greenish gray turf, brownish gray turf to light gray sandy beds and very minor part of shale. The also bear grades of laminated black and green thin coal seams and minor thin beds of grey to greenish siltstones, minor to moderate poor degree of soft, microplastic, fine to medium, with glauconite inclusion sots.\n\nCement.GEOLOGICAL WELL REPORT\n\n1. Circulation condition drilled from 115.0 to 245.0 m, prepared pit and drilled to 503.5 m, circulate hole clean and slug heavy pill, POOH to surface - run in 8 \xc2\xbd" PDC bit to bottom, circulated hole clean, dropped into and performed flow check, pump slug heavy pill, POOH\n2) Rig up Weatherford tools and casing elements, performed hydraulic meeting, RIH 13 3/8" casing to bottom, casing shoe to 499.0m. Make up B.J. cement float tools and drop plug, pump 300 sx slurry cementing plugs displaced with 180m 8 gal mud; Bump plug and released pressure. Check floats bump plug and land line.\n3) Nipple up well head. Rig up 13 5/8" BOP stack and land line, perform pressure tests - OK. RIH and tag cement.\n4) Make up bit and used 12 \xc2\xbc" BHA; RIH to 458.0 m, used string weights, drilled to 512.0 m, circulated and changed pressure tool to 585.0 m; circulating and conditioning performing to 600.0 m, continued drilling and drilled to 480.0 m. Circulate and change BHA, make up LOL-PHPL mud, commence displacement circulate mud displaced and hole to 503.0 m; POOH circulated hole clean and dropped bit and string weights.\n5) 12 1/4" hole: made up 12 \xc2\xbc" BHA RIH to 503.5 m with blindbox to 512.0 m, circulate and perform flow check. run drill pipe, perform formation test.O.K.\n6) Drilled from surface to 300 m. Make up 12 \xc2\xbc" PDC bit, RIH tag bottom, perform flow checks and drill to 720.0 m, circulated and performed slips and drilled to 750.0 m; drilled to 825.0 m, circulated heavy concentration drilling 875.0 m., continued drilling to 905.0 m, perform changing drilling parameters and using mud of drilling and wt. Retained on 930 m, continued drilling with conditioner perform and reamer; despite mixing SLS cement plugged hole to 972.0. m\n7) Performed reamer operation BHA, drilled to 972.0 m, circulated and removing tool and drilled plug cement displaced; cement recovered to 400 Psi and circulated, continue drilling and drilling from 1000.0 m to 1100.0 m.\n8) Wiper trip & conditioning hole; recondition circulate and condition hole to 1150.0 m, POOH to 102.0 m, and run LOL-PHPL, condition circulate and clean hole.\n\nNOTE: Tag bottom, run logs, circulation coincide 2071 09 101 - 102,\n\xe2\x80\xa2 Total depth, unconditional RIH, circulate bottom up perform Flow check, pump slug heavy pill, POOHTOTAL AUSTRAL \xc2\xbb                   \xc2\xab EL Martillo -x-1/1 \xc2\xbb                 \xc2\xab SAC .EMa-x-1/1 \xc2\xbb\n\n                          GEOLOGICAL REPORT\n                               CONTENTS\n\nDistribution list\n\n1. FORM.\n\n\nCorrelalion with: L: LORD-4 LAGUNA DE ORD 4C02K-1 CANADON CAMUS1 NORTE X-1            \n                                                                                          Log depth origin : RT                                                                                                                                                                    \n                                                                                                            TVD RT MSSL: 54.85 m\n\n\nValidaled on:\n16-AugusI-91                                                         By: A.GUIDI- D.PEREZ\n.10.2 Lithology\n\nPatagonia Formation (607.5 - 879.5 mTVD)\nThis Formation is represented by greenish gray siltstone and claystone, dark greenish gray, blocky and massive. With gray white tuffaceous lenses, with lithic grains, pyrite, mica, and minor to. not. interbeds of dark greenish gray sandstone intercalated towards the top in thin beds and as fine laminas. These are in turbidite sequences occasional tabular to lenticular geometry. With occasional brown carbonaceous gypsum, to black reworking fragments. Bioturbation, parallel laminations present in, quartz, mica, and pyrite filled, to abundant, in pack greenish gray tuffaceous siltstone. In sandstones. Pilotandstone fragments occur as lithic, Mm to throughout the base. They are partly. micritic, locally subblocky, blocky moderately hard. Shell fragments\n\nRio Leona Formation (879.5 - 1104 mTVD)\nThis Formation is composed mainly by greenish gray shale. These are subtabular, irregular fracture, micaceous, tuffaceous with pyrite, blocky, glauconal green-dark lakes, in part sandy, fine soft to grading to greywacke, litharenite. Iron, boulders of dark green clay in thin bedded limestone, few white fragments, sand fossils, lenses. clumps cyclical, plant slices sands, matrix, friable, poor porous top of. Coarse grained sandstones with penetrative beddings and silty laminations, and cross-stratifications in the lenses, light brownish to light reddish, with brown due to argilaceous silica-poor to subblocky, firm to soft.\n\nMan Aike Formation-Margosa Inferior-Senonian (1100 - 1408.4 mTVD)\nThis unit has two intervals. In the Upper 1100 to 1220 mTVD, dark greenish grey shales, minor lenses and subtabular, with pyritic, mica, toufaceous with glauconite, and in part fine to very fine litharenite. Towards 1200 m section with several lenses, circles parallel o wave good porous. Lower 1220 to the final depth of 1408.4 in very fine grained heavy mineral laminations to no pyritic, white coarse glauconitic sandstone and hard red. In contacts base with friable claystones, quartz, and black carbonaceous shingles, light sandstone with argillaceous-silty lenses. Argillaceous and to glauconaceous sediments interbedding dark green shaly formations. In partly soft to firm. In part blocky to subblocky siltstone, fracture, with carbonaceous mantles micaceous, tufaceous. sands, soft to blocky.The Lower unit (1220 m to 1293 m ) is formed , mainly by medium gray to dark greenish gray siltstone, blocky, firm to soft, sandy, with quartz & glauconite inclusions, rare calcareous and sideritic cement, faint to distinct parallel and graded greenish gray sandy laminae. Rare gray, very fine, soft, massive sandstones with glauconite, abundant argillaceous matrix, friable to loose, partly calcified. Thickness of 18.58m. Well debris poorly massive-lard.\n\n- Anita Formation (1440 - 1538.7m MD)\n\nThis formation can be divided in two intervals. The upper section (1538-1441m) is formed mainly by light gray sandstone, medium to fine, well sorted, subrounded, quartz, siltstone, abundant trace fossils, fair porosity, blocky, partly calcified, fair visible porosity. Minor very fine greenish, gray, hard silty sandstone with faint brownish laminae.\nThe lower interval (1440 - 1501 m) is represented by olive gray silty-claystone, massive, blocky, fissile, abundant fossil hash. Partly calcified matrix.\n\n- Altavista Formation (1538.7 - 1653 m MD)\n\nIt is represented basically by olive gray silty-claystone, massive, blocky, irregular fracture, soft, plastic, tight, grading to claystone. The formation lower section (1654 m - 1580 m) is composed of black to olive gray siltstone and diamictite, massive, blocky, firm. There is also the presence of dark greenish gray argillites and siltstone, very fine to fine, well sorted, massive, shaly fissile beds of laminated tectorum claystone with abundant forams nodules. Black to brownish-g ay. Thin beds of urite.\n\n-Mata Amarilla (1563 - 1927.9 mMD)\n\nThis formation is represented basically by olive gray, silty-claystone, massive, blocky, irregular fracture, soft, plastic, tight. grading to claystone. The lower section (1300 - 1650m) is composed of dark gray argillite with soft to hard, well sorted, subrounded, quartz, siltstone, shaly siltstone, fair porosity. Poor fossil preservation, multiple laminations of silty shale in the upper part of the section. Thin layers of limestone, light brownish gray, massive, oolitic, vuggy, moderate hard.Toward the base, sandstone, medium gray to light gray, very fine to fine or medium grained, well\nshorted, quartz, green lithics, tuffaceous matrix, calcareous cement, friable, poor porosity, are\nrecovered in the well.\n\nPiedra Clavada (1927.9 - 2204 mMD)\n\nThis unit can be separated in three intervals. The Upper section (1939-2070m), is represented by\nvery light gray and gray sandstone, very fine to fine grained, medium well sorted orthoquartzite,\nquartz, green lithics, tuffaceous matrix, calcareous cement, carbonaceous materials and coal debris,\nfriable, fair to poor porosity. At 2040-2058m beds of light gray shale of fine grained, laminated , in part\nconglomeratic, poorly sorted, subangular grains, lithics, scarce tuffaceous materials, calcareous\ncement, firm, toward upper contact sandstone layers, thin interbeds of shale, dark gray, massive,\nblocky, fissile, clay parting. \n\nThe Middle Section (2040-2164m) beds of light gray shale of fine grained, moderately hard to\nvery hard condition graded to medium to coarse, gray, subrounded, quartz, green lithics,\nabundant feldspathic matrix, friable to poor porosity.\n\nThe Lower Section at 2164m rocks composed of gray sandstone, medium to fine, volcaniclastic\ndebris, subrounded to rounded grains of quartz, lithics, abundant feldspar, fair porosity. Thin\nbeds of light gray shale with pyrite, carbonaceous debris, argillaceous matrix, firm to very firm\ncondition. Upper contact with ignimbrite layers, zones of bipyramids, reaction, firm. Toward\nbasement shale of light gray to medium brownish gray limestone, massive, dense, disaggregated,\nsubangular, quartz, green lithics.\n\nKachalithe (2204 m - 2755.6 mMD)\n\nThis Formation is represented by light gray and gray to brownish gray shale, massive, fissile,\nfriable to very firm, medium condition. Thin levels of gray sandstone, massive, blocky, occasional\nglauconite debris, in part conglomeratic, with quartz, rock lithics, abundant feldspar, firm. \nIn the lower part intervals of gray to dark gray limestone, compact, firm, dense, slightly \ncalcareous. Occasionally tuff with pyrite. No productive zones within it.\n\nRio Mayer Sup (2755.9 m \xe2\x80\x93 2755.9 m mMD)\n\nThis Formation is composed of three different lithological units: \nUpper Interval of light gray to medium gray shale, massive, blocky, slightly calcareous,\nwith low calcareous contents, coally firm, fossils, soft firm. Thin levels of white to medium gray tuff\nwith pyrite intervals.blocky, subplaty, massive, firm to soft, with quartzose nodules. Thin levels of light brownish gray to brownish gray limestone, blocky, micritic, hard\nThe Middle interval is represented by light gray calcareous shale, blocky to subplaty, irregularly fractured, massive, strong calcareous structure; with plant root grading to light brownish gray to gray clayey limestone. Soft thin beds of brownish gray limestone above with white veins of calcite (in sparry crystals) are present at the base.\nThe lower interval is represented by shale, medium gray, massive, soft, with little calcareous contents, locally firm. Thin beds of brownish gray of limestone, massive, compact, in angular fracture, smooth, soft to hard. \n\n- Rio Mayer Fm: (2756.9 - 2840.9 m MD)\n\nDark gray to black bioturbated argillaceous (with glauconite) massive firm gray and black siltstone, blocky, irregular fracture, microbire dominated; weakly calcareous, in frequencies interbedded thinly bedded of calcite, locally fine to medium quartz grains inclisions, firm to hard, in part grading to gray black clayey limestones. Toward the base, frequent concretion horizons black in part grades down to more than shale, blocky, moderately compact, marine to freshwater fossils, with gloss-gelatinous aspect. Sparse grainstone with floating grains, in subangular to subrounded mixture of pyrite. Local hard beds in stylolometry, firm to compact microcalcakes, fairly massive, blocky to irregularly fractured. Sections are sharply fractured and microparting. Firm to not massive, weakly compacted silt and fine sandstone with discontinuous quartz wavy parallel light gray sandstones, massive, weakly Compact, rarely glauconitic. Stable contacts, fine to coarse, fairly sorted, fine to coarse grains quartz sand to silty lower black gray shales grading in thin beds from massive, friable to brownish loose argillite.\n\n- Springhill (2840.9 - 2970.1m MD)\n\nArgo Sequence (2836.5 - 2840.9 m)\n\nThe sequence composed of thick dark sandstone, very light gray, hyaline, medium to coarse moderately compact grains, microbire disseminated, with quartzite nodules, firm, friable to loose with stability. Downward becomes fine in a mixture of clay illite, minor argillaceous-lithic fragments, hard.\nHidra Sequence (2970.1 m to TD)\n\nThe springhill (2840.9 - 2880m), in composed by very light gray sandstones-dull facies structure, fine to poorly sorted, subangular to subrounded, quartz, hyaline, scarce argillaceous -uffucumous to macro, the argillaceous from 2840.9 - 2970.1 m to the \xe0\xa4\xad\xe0\xa4\xbe\xe0\xa4\xb0\xe0\xa5\x80 sandstones --frequently massive facies, transition tofriable to loose, fair porosity. Interbeds of siltstone, medium dark gray to brownish black, massive, blocky, medium dark gray to brownish black, massive, blocky, quartz, glauconite inclusions, coal clasts, clay debris, moderate calcareous reaction.\nThin layers of claystone, very light gray, fine to very fine, in part medium well, soft with mica interbeds of siltstone, quartz, glauconite, argillaceous-tuffaceous matrix, moderate consolidate, poor porosity.\nD 120 \xe2\x80\x94 Tobifera (2889.7 \xe2\x80\x94 2970.1 m)\nThe basal interval (2890.0 \xe2\x80\x94 2989.4 m), is represented by very light sandstone, fine to medium downward sequence) medium to coarse, fair sorted, angular to subangular, quartz, glauconite, volcanic rock fragments, argillaceous matrix, washed out, loose to friable, fair porosity. Coal level at 2902.0  subblocky to subcolloids, conchoidal fracture, impregnability vacuum, moderately hard Intercalations of siltstone, medium dark gray, massive, blocky, glauconite clots, coal debris, pyrite, moderately consolidated, bioturbation is weak to fair. Thin layers of claystone very light gray, massive with friable levels, subcolloids structure, coal debris, massive, blocky.\nSiltstone, medium dark, massive, medium light gray, fine to very fine, poorly sorted, quartz, tuff matrix, friable, low to poor consolidate porosity.\n\xc2\xb7 Tobifera (2970.1 \xe2\x80\x94 2990m MD)\nThis Formation is composed of interlocations of medium dark gray tuffaceous sandstone, fine to very fine, very poor sorted, subcolloids, quartz hyaline, minor lithics, micropyrite, and abundant tuffaceous matrix, friable, fair porosity. Interlevels of claystone, medium gray, massive, subplanar, with coal-prite, firm. Downward full blocky to very light gray pyrite, massive, earthy, and massive, subvious aspect, hard.SANTA CRUZ I\nSTRATIGRAPHIC COLUMN\n\n                    AGE Including samples from 6\xe2\x80\x99\n\tShale debris                           - TOTAL AUSTRAL -                           *  EL MARTILLO, x-1 / 1 -                                          *  SAC.EMa.x-1# *\n\n                                                  1.1 General summary\n\nThe Santa Cruz 1 block is located in the northern part of the Austral basin (figure 1). The\nprospect lies in the eastern edge of the block, only few kilometers eastwards from the\nLaguna del Oro, La Paz, Campo Boleadoras, Campo Indio oil and gas fields.\n\nObjectives\n\nThe main objective of the El Martillo x-1 well was to investigate the Springhill (Apg Srg and\nHilda Sequences), principal Jurassic reservoir in the area, the well was located within\nan embracing antiform (confirmed by 2D seismic).\n\n* As secondary objectives, the following intervals may be interesting: basal tertiary\n  sandstone, Aalen fm.,sandstones, Piedra Clavada Fm. Sandstone and top Tobifera tuff (if\n  all reservoirs are viable).\n\n                                                    1.2 MAIN RESULTS\n\nThe main data and results obtained from the El Martillo x-1 well can be summarized as \nfollows:\n                                                \n                                                 Findings\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2 The Argo and Hilda sequences are water bearing: from MDT pretests and fluids\n   samples (argon at depth interval 2,498.1 m, 2,566) (Hilde: 2753 / 59 m)\n\xe2\x80\xa2 A water sample was recovered by segregation in the Argo Sands\n   (2,498.1 m 615 API GRAD m = 41,4460 ppm Measured salinity)\n\xe2\x80\xa2 No appreciable hydrocarbon effects were observed within the Hilda sequence by MDT\n   pretests (2,566 m).\n\xe2\x80\xa2 All resin are water table.260-270   26    SANDSTONE  dark yellowish brown (10YR 4/4) to dark brown (10YR 3/3), fine        \n                      grained, subrounded, siliceous cement, calcareous inter-clasts, fossiliferous\n                      (fragments).\n270-280   30    LIMESTONE  wackestone to pack limestone (10YR 4/3) , light gray (N7), fossiliferous\n                      (10YR 5/6 and 10YR 6/3), calcareous cement.\n280-290   31    CLAYSTONE  pale yellowish brown (10YR 6/2), black, soft, plastic, blocky, shale.\n                      SILTSTONE  very pale brown (10YR 8/2), pale yellowish brown, soft, blocky, thin-bedded\n                      (1 1/2 in.).\nTR          26   \n290-302   38    CLAYSTONE  dark yellowish brown (10YR 4/2), black, soft, plastic, fossiliferous (shell),\n                      siliceous cement, blocky.\n302-306   28    SILTSTONE  faint yellowish brown (10YR 7/2), orange (10YR 6/2), with calcareous cement,\n                      fossiliferous (fragments), thin-bedded (2 in.). Downward the sandstone becomes fine to very fine quartz, abundant glauconite matrix, limonite and ferric siliceous cement, silicified, poorly sorted. At the base of the upper sandstone a coal layer was observed.\n\nBajo Pescado is 114.5 m thick and is composed of 17.8 medium to coarse grained, well sorted, poorly sorted, argillaceous - tuffaceous matrix, interlayers of siltstone and limonite, clayish, siliceous cement, silicified, limonite and glauconite matrix. The sandstone becomes downward it becomes coarse. Intercalation of shale and siltstone, massive, blocky, pyritic, coal debris. Coal level. Toward base tuffaceous sandstone, fine to very fine, poorly sorted.\n\nPetrophysics\n\n                                                                                                                                                                                                22002-2010 6 "COAL (CONT\'D):" Sandstone, light gray (N7. 5/0), silty, micaceous; poor gas show.\n2020-2029.5 9.5 SANDSTONE: poor gas show, quartz 94-95%, some feld 5%, some clay\n                        cement [sandstone maybe oolite].\n\n2051-2058 7 CHERT: various colors, light gray (N8/0)-light green (GLEY 1 3/10G), dolointr in part, micaceous; rare organic matter, small quantity, of green, silt-size minerals; no show.\n2069-2070 .5 SANDSTONE:gray (N5/N6), medium, small qtz grains, micaceous, calcareous; no fluorescence, no show.\n\n2075-2077 2 SANDSTONE: brownish light gray (10 YR 6/1), qtz 90-95%, mica 5%, iron stained, micaceous and calcareous, siltstone stringers and lenses; no show.\n\n2079-2089 10 SANDSTONE: quartzitic, good show, quartz 95%, micaceous; gas show probably water or shoe leather effect, gas show, silica bonded.\n\n2090-2095 5 SANDSTONE: various colors, mostly brownish light gray (10 YR 6/1); quartz 95%, feldspar 5%, well cemented with quartz overgrowths, minor iron oxide cement, silt size particles roughly 10 to 15%.\n\n2104-2110 6 CLAYSTONE: medium brownish gray (5 YR 4/1), ferromagnesian minerals, feldspar, mica, micaceous.\n\n2109-2112 3 SANDSTONE: quartzitic, grains of quartz I/5/0), micaceous, calcareous, thin lenses of gray limestone SILICIFIED; poor gas show in transition zone (mostly shaly).\n\n2110-2111 1 CLAVOO:t, smt iron Eotriso& 5hscaitioePoht, 7 ccitllA matrix, Mowdarglor chopped fine sews :\n                        No oil shows.\n\n2112-2117 5 CHEB% down gray! OBJECTIVES\n\n- The basal Tertiary sandstone, Anita Fm sandstones and Piedra Clavada Fm basal sandstone wedge, although of good reservoir quality, had no trapped hydrocarbons.\n\n- The encountered reservoirs belonging to Argo and Hidra sequences, had dead oil shows.
